<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio FREQUENCY IDENTIFICATION (RFID) systems have recently attracted much attention due to their potential capability in supply chain management and retail item management. In the passive RFID system, the reader transmits a continuous-wave (CW) RF signal to tags and receives the backscattered signal from tags, simultaneously. The transmitted CW signal may be directly coupled to the receiving part of the reader to degrade the receiving sensitivity. Therefore, the high isolation between the transmitting and receiving parts is very critical for the RFID performance <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>.</p><p>Three different solutions for achieving sufficient Tx/Rx isolation are the use of separate transmission and receiving antennas, the use of a circulator and the use of a directional coupler <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Separate transmitting and receiving antennas enable high isolation but require more space within the design. Isolation between separate transmitting and receiving antennas highly depends on mutual alignments and radiation patterns of the antennas. By enlarging the space between the antennas, the isolation is improved <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>.</p><p>In this paper, we present a new method to diminish the minimum of distance between the antennas while improving isolation. Two concentric, circularly polarized antennas and the 4-points feed circuits which make the same circular polarization are proposed. The high isolation between the transmitting and receiving parts is verified by the circuit model and theoretical analysis for the proposed antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna with Circulator</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a> shows the geometry of the proposed integrated antenna with circulator, which consists of two QSAs (a set of four inner inverted-F antennas and a set of four outer inverted-F antennas) and feed circuits. Each QSA is designed to have right-hand circular polarization characteristic and two QSAs are arranged concentrically.</p><p>Consider the block diagram of Tx/Rx as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a>. The two equivalent 5-port feed circuits and one equivalent 8-port network representing the mutual coupling between feeder_Tx and feeder_Rx are cascaded. We suppose the ideal power division of the 5-port feed circuit is the same amplitude, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 2.285em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.99em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">â</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-6" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">6.0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{-}6.0</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dB, but different phase, 0, 90, 180, and 270 degrees for each output port, respectively. = \left[\matrix{ M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{1}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{2}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{3}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{4}}} \cr M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{4}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{1}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{2}}} &amp; M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{3}}} \cr M_{R_{1}}{_{T_{3}}} &amp; This concept can be applied to any structures having the feed and antennas placed concentrically and identically circulating.

These results mean that the proposed concept for the isolation is insensitive with the distance of two antennas.<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Fabrication of the Proposed AntennaWith Circulator</h2></div><p>In this chapter, the proposed structure including antennas is fabricated using the feed circuits of the previous chapter. A two-step procedure was used to design the antenna having RFID Tx/Rx path isolation characteristics. The first step is to design one antenna for inner path (Tx QSA) and another for outer path (Rx QSA) individually and measure the gain of each antenna. The second step is to concentrically incorporate them on the same ground. All simulations are performed with the help of the CST</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/4446029/4476051/4476051-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/4446029/4476051/4476051-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig><p>(a) Fabricated antenna and measured radiation patterns at 910 MHz. (b)Rx QSA. (c) Tx QSA:âRHCP radiation, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1019" role="math" style="width: 1.591em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.26em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.921em 1001.19em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1020"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1021"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1022"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1023" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.202em;">â¦</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">{}\ldots</script></tex-math></inline-formula> LHCP radiation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4476051/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>Microwave Studio. The proposed antenna is mounted on a grounded FR-4 substrate with thickness of 0.5 mm, relative permittivity of 4.5, and size of 130<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1024" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.38em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1025"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1026"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1027"></span></span><span class="mspace" id="MathJax-Span-1028" style="height: 0.003em; vertical-align: 0.003em; width: 0.183em; display: inline-block; overflow: hidden;"></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1029" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">Ã</span><span class="mspace" id="MathJax-Span-1030" style="height: 0.003em; vertical-align: 0.003em; width: 0.183em; display: inline-block; overflow: hidden;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">{}\,\times\,</script></tex-math></inline-formula>130 mm<sup>2</sup>. The line widths are 2 mm for Tx QSA and 3 mm for Rx QSA. The heights are 30 mm for both Tx and Rx.<p></p><p>The distance between two QSA is 24 mm (see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1</a>), which corresponds to about 0.07 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1031" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1032"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1033"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1034"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1035" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Î»</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{}\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> approximately. To increase the input impedance of the QSA, a shorted matching line in each inverted-F antenna in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_3">[4]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_3">[5]</a> is used. The distance between one inverted-F antenna and a matching line is chosen to be 7 mm for the inner QSA and 23 mm for the outer QSA. The height of the matching line is designed to be 6 mm (Tx QSA) and 9 mm (Rx QSA).</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Measurement Results</h2></div><p>In the following results, the S-parameters have been measured for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1036" role="math" style="width: 5.048em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.508em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.45em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1037"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1038"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1039" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1040"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1041"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1042" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1043" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1044" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">50</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1045" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1046" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î©</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">Z_{0} =50\ \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> reference. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a>, the measured gain of antennas fabricated individually is about 2 dBi for the Tx QSA and about 1.8 dBi for the Rx QSA at 910 MHz. 3-dB beamwidth is about 114Â° for both antennas.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a> shows the measured and simulated isolations between the Tx QSA and the Rx QSA for the proposed reader antenna. The antenna has high Tx/Rx isolation more than 43 dB at center frequency. The return loss for each antenna has less than 20 dB for the entire frequency range (860â960 MHz). In the radiation pattern and axial ratio (AR) measurements, one QSA is fed and the other QSA is loaded by a matched termination. The AR and the gain of the antenna are measured at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1047" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1053" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; <div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A novel design of the RFID reader antenna with circular polarization and high Tx/Rx isolation characteristics in UHF RFID band has been presented. By using a novel feeder connection method, the RFID front-end can have high isolation characteristics. The experimental results show that the Tx/Rx path isolation of about 40 dB has been achieved. The presented antenna has 0.7 dBi and 1 dBi Tx/Rx antenna gains.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
